Seventh Proof: Duration is Contingent (Incomplete)
The author begins a proof that time is contingent because it is composed of successive contingent parts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the beginning of the seventh proof that duration (time) is contingent because it is composed of successive contingent parts.

Core Idea
Duration's contingent parts prove its own contingency.

The author presents a concise proof: if something is composed of parts that are each contingent, the whole must also be contingent. Here he applies it to duration (time), arguing that since time is made up of successive moments that come into being and pass away, time itself cannot be necessary. This lesson examines the first premises of this proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation. Notice the abrupt ending.
The text is cut off mid-sentence, but the premises are clear.
2
Identify the two premises
The proof has two premises: (1) duration is composed of successive parts, and (2) each part is contingent (hadith). Recognize how these premises support the claim that duration is possible in itself.
3
Consider the intended conclusion
Ask yourself what conclusion the author likely intended. Based on typical kalam reasoning, if the parts are contingent, the whole is contingent, so duration must be contingent and not eternal.
The completed argument would appear on the following page.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة السابعة : هذه المدة ممكنة لذاتها . بدليل : أنها مركبة من الأجزاء المتعاقبة ، وكل واحد من تلك الأجزاء المتعاقبة المتتالية حادث ، وكل حادث
The seventh proof: This duration is possible in itself. Evidence: it is composed of successive parts, and every one of those successive consecutive parts is contingent, and every contingent...
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage begins the seventh proof, arguing that duration (al-midda) is contingent (mumkin) in itself. The author states two premises: (1) duration is composed of successive parts; (2) each of those parts is contingent (hadith). The argument is cut off, but the intended conclusion is likely that duration is contingent, hence cannot be necessary or a condition for God's existence. The proof structure is typical of kalam: if something is composed of contingent parts, the whole is contingent. However, the text ends mid-sentence on page 15. The complete argument would need to be sought on the following page.

Key Terms
مدة
ممكن
حادث
أجزاء متعاقبة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the proof denies the reality of time
Correction: The proof does not deny the reality of time; it argues that time is created and contingent, not eternal and necessary.

Checkpoint
According to the seventh proof, what evidence is given for duration being possible in itself?
A) Duration is eternal.
B) Duration is composed of successive contingent parts.
C) Duration is indivisible.
D) Duration is necessary.

Key Takeaway
Duration is contingent because it is composed of successive contingent parts.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If time is a created, contingent reality, then why do you treat your hours as if they belong to you rather than to the One who made them? How would your today be different if you truly believed every moment is a gift from the Necessarily Existent?
?
What one activity in your daily routine is most driven by the illusion that time is infinite or yours to control? How can you intentionally submit that activity to the Creator of time right now?
?
The proof argues that because each successive part of duration is contingent, the whole must be contingent. Does your heart attach itself to the fleeting moments or to the Eternal One behind them? What concrete step can you take tonight to anchor your hope in what does not pass away?

Why Priority and Posteriority Do Not Depend on Time
Proof that time is contingent and priority/posteriority are time-independent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the proof that time is contingent and that priority and posteriority can be understood without reference to time.

Core Idea
Priority and posteriority are intrinsic to events, not dependent on time.

This passage presents a sophisticated proof by contradiction to show that priority and posteriority do not require time. The argument first establishes that time, if it exists, is contingent. Then it shows that if priority/posteriority depended on time, assuming time's non-existence would lead to a contradiction. The conclusion is that these relational concepts are independent of time.

Guided Path
1
Understand the first part: contingency of time
The argument begins by showing that each part of time is possible, so time itself is possible. Grasp this reasoning.
The key is that the whole depends on parts which are contingent.
2
Follow the proof by contradiction
The argument assumes that priority/posteriority require time. Then it shows this leads to a contradiction: assuming time's non-existence would require its existence.
Focus on the logical steps: if priority/posteriority need time, then even when time is assumed nonexistent, it must exist to ground the relation.
3
Conclude the independence
The contradiction proves the assumption false, so priority/posteriority do not depend on time. See how this conclusion follows.
The conclusion is that these concepts are grounded in the events themselves.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ممكن ، فإذن كل واحد من أجزاء الزمان ممكن الوجود لذاته ، ومجموعه مفتقر إلى كل واحد من أجزائه ، والمفتقر في وجوده إلى ما يكون ممكن الوجود لذاته، كان أولى أن يكون ممكن الوجود لذاته. فثبت : أن المدة والزمان - بتقدير أن يكون موجوداً - كان ممكن الوجود لذاته ، وكل ما كان ممكن الوجود لذاته ، فإنه لا يلزم من فرض عدمه بعد وجوده محال . إذا ثبت هذا فنقول : لو كانت هذه البعدية لا يعقل تقررها ، إلا بسبب الزمان ، فحينئذ يلزم كون الزمان موجوداً ، حال ما فرض معدوماً ، لأن عدمه بعد وجوده لما لم يتقرر إلا بالزمان، فلو فرضنا أنه عدم بعد وجوده، فحينئذ يلزم من فرض كون هذا العدم حاصلاً ، بعد ذلك الوجود، أن يكون الزمان موجوداً ، حال ما فرضناه معدوماً ، فثبت : أنه لو كان الزمان موجوداً ، لكان يلزم من مجرد فرض عدمه، فرض وجوده ، وهذا محال . فثبت : أن فرض عدم الزمان يوجب المحال لذاته، وكل ما كان كذلك كان واجباً لذاته فالزمان بتقدير كونه موجوداً ، يلزم بحسب الاعتبار الأول أن يكون ممكناً ، وبحسب الاعتبار الثاني أن يكون واجباً لذاته. ولما كان ذلك محالاً ، ثبت : أن حصول هذه القبليات، والبعديات لا يتوقف على وجود المدة والزمان . وهو المطلوب
Possible. Then each one of the parts of time is possible in itself, and its whole is dependent on each of its parts, and that which is dependent in its existence on that which is possible in itself is more deserving of being possible in itself. So it is established that duration and time—if they exist—are possible in themselves. And everything that is possible in itself, it is not necessary that assuming its non-existence after its existence leads to an impossibility. If this is established, we say: If this posteriority is not conceivable except by means of time, then it would be necessary that time exists at the moment we assume it non-existent, because its non-existence after its existence is not determined except by time. So if we assume that it is non-existent after its existence, then it follows from assuming that this non-existence occurs after that existence that time exists at the moment we assume it non-existent. So it is established that if time existed, then from merely assuming its non-existence, its existence would be assumed, and this is impossible. So it is established that assuming the non-existence of time necessitates an impossibility in itself, and everything that is like that is necessary in itself. So time, if it is assumed to exist, necessitates by the first consideration that it is possible, and by the second consideration that it is necessary in itself. And since that is impossible, it is established that the obtaining of these priorities and posteriorities does not depend on the existence of duration and time. That is the desired conclusion.
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage is a proof by contradiction (burhan khalfi) to show that time is not necessary for the concepts of priority and posteriority. The argument begins by establishing that time and duration, if they exist, are contingent (mumkin al-wujud) because their parts are contingent. Then it proceeds: if priority and posteriority (i.e., before and after) could only be realized through time, then time would have to exist even at the moment we assume it to be non-existent. This leads to a contradiction: assuming time's non-existence would require its existence. Therefore, the assumption that time is necessary for priority and posteriority is false. The conclusion is that priority and posteriority are intrinsic to events themselves, not dependent on time.

Key Terms
زمان (time)
مدة (duration)
ممكن الوجود (contingent existence)
واجب الوجود (necessary existence)
قبليات (priorities)
بعديات (posteriorities)
محال (impossible)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That priority and posteriority require time to be meaningful.
Correction: The proof shows that such a dependence leads to a contradiction, so priority and posteriority are intrinsic to events themselves.

Checkpoint
According to the argument, if time were assumed to be non-existent, what follows?
A) Time becomes necessary.
B) Assuming time's non-existence leads to the assumption of its existence, which is contradictory.
C) Priority and posteriority vanish.
D) Time remains contingent.

Key Takeaway
Priority and posteriority are not dependent on time; they are intrinsic to the events themselves.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever assumed that time is necessary for something to be 'before' or 'after'? Does this argument challenge your daily reliance on time as the ultimate measure?
?
If priority and posteriority are independent of time, how should that affect the way you prioritize your life—especially your eemaan and actions that have eternal consequences beyond time?
?
Are you living as though time is the only frame for your goals, or are you recognizing that some priorities (like your relationship with Allah) transcend time entirely?

Priority and Posteriority Are Intrinsic, Not from Time
Refutes the claim that priority and posteriority require time using the philosophers' own admission.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the philosophers' own admission about the intrinsic nature of precedence in originated things actually refutes their claim that priority and posteriority require time.

Core Idea
Priority and posteriority are intrinsic to things, not dependent on time.

The philosophers claim that the originated thing's being after non-existence is intrinsic and not caused externally. Yet they also say priority and posteriority require time. The author points out this contradiction, arguing that if precedence is intrinsic, it cannot be dependent on an external entity like time.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and note the philosophers' admission
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the philosophers' statement that the originated thing's being after non-existence is necessarily established in itself and not from a separate cause.
This admission is key to the argument.
2
Identify the contradiction
The author asks: if precedence is intrinsic, how can they claim priority/posteriority depend on time? Locate this rhetorical question in the passage.
The contradiction lies between the philosophers' admission and their later claim.
3
Understand the author's exposition
The author explains that a thing judged to be before or after another cannot exist without that priority or posteriority. This shows these attributes are intrinsic, not added by an external cause.
The author uses the property of the necessary in itself to strengthen the argument.
4
Reach the conclusion
The conclusion is that priority and posteriority cannot depend on an external entity like time. Affirm this understanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثامنة : إن الحكماء قالوا : المحدث له عدم سابق ، وله وجود لاحق ، وله آن وجوده حصل بعد عدمه. ثم قالوا : إن كونه بعد العدم ، يمتنع أن يكون مستفاداً من سبب منفصل ، لأن كون هذا الوجود مسبوقاً بذلك العدم، أمر واجب الثبوت لذاته ، ولعينه ، فإنه من المحال فرض هذا الوجود ، إلا مسبوقاً بالعدم، ولما كانت هذه المسبوقية أمراً واجب الثبوت لهذا المحدث لذاته ولعينه ، امتنع أن يكون مستفاداً من سبب منفصل . وأقول : هذا اعتراف من هؤلاء الأفاضل بأن كون هذا الوجود موصوفاً بأنه بعد العدم ، أمر لا يمكن أن يكون معللاً بغيره ، وإذا كان الأمر كذلك ، فكيف قالوا ههنا : إن هذه القبلية وهذه البعدية لا يتقرر واحد منها ، إلا لأجل شيء مغاير يسمى بالمدة والزمان ؟ وتمام تقريره : أن الشيء المحكوم عليه بأنه قبل غيره يمتنع تقرر وجوده إلا مع هذه القبلية . والشيء المحكوم عليه بأنه بعد غيره ، يمنع تقرره إلا مع هذه البعدية . فثبت : أن حصول هذه القبليات، وهذه البعديات ، أمور ثابتة لهذه الأشياء لذواته ولأعيانها . ثم ثبت في خواص الواجب لذاته ، وخواص الممكن : أن الواجب لذاته ، يمتنع أن يكون واجباً لغيره ، وهذا ينتج أن حصول هذه القبليات والبعديات ، يمتنع أن تكون موقوفة على موجود آخر مغاير والله أعلم .
The eighth argument: The philosophers said: The originated (al-muhdath) has a prior non-existence, a later existence, and an instant when its existence occurs after its non-existence. Then they said: Its being after non-existence cannot be derived from a separate cause, because this existence being preceded by that non-existence is a matter necessarily established in itself and for its own essence, for it is impossible to assume this existence except as preceded by non-existence. And since this precedence is a matter necessarily established for this originated thing in itself and for its own essence, it cannot be derived from a separate cause. And I say: This is an admission from these eminent ones that this existence being described as after non-existence is a matter that cannot be caused by another. And if this is the case, how can they say here that this priority and this posteriority are not determined one of them except by reason of something other called duration and time? And the full exposition: that the thing judged to be before another, the determination of its existence is impossible except with this priority. And the thing judged to be after another, its determination is prevented except with this posteriority. So it is established that the obtaining of these priorities and these posteriorities are matters established for these things in themselves and for their own essences. Then it is established in the properties of the necessary in itself and the properties of the contingent: that the necessary in itself cannot be necessary for another. And this yields that the obtaining of these priorities and posteriorities cannot be dependent on another existent other. And God knows best.
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer argument (refutation) against the philosophers who claim that priority and posteriority require time. The author (the commentator) begins by citing the philosophers' own position: the originated thing (muhdath) has a prior non-existence and a later existence, and its being after non-existence is intrinsic, not caused externally. He then points out that this admission contradicts their later claim that priority and posteriority depend on time. The argument continues by affirming that priority and posteriority are intrinsic to things themselves, and since the necessary in itself cannot be caused by another, these attributes cannot be dependent on an external entity like time.

Key Terms
محدث (originated)
عدم سابق (prior non-existence)
مسبوقية (precedence)
واجب الثبوت (necessarily established)
علة (cause)
مغاير (other/separate)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that priority and posteriority are relational attributes that require an external measure like time.
Correction: The argument shows they are intrinsic to the things themselves, not dependent on an external entity.

Checkpoint
What did the philosophers admit according to the eighth argument?
A) Priority and posteriority depend on time.
B) The originated thing's being after non-existence is intrinsic and not caused externally.
C) Time is necessary for existence.
D) The necessary in itself can be caused by another.

Key Takeaway
Priority and posteriority are intrinsic attributes of things, not dependent on an external entity like time.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The philosophers admitted that the attribute of being-after-non-existence is intrinsic, yet they still sought an external cause in time. Where in your own life do you know something is true about yourself—like your accountability for your actions—yet you still look for external excuses or circumstances to explain it away?
?
If priority and posteriority are intrinsic, then the order of your deeds and their consequences is not merely a matter of time but a real quality of those deeds. How does this deepen your sense of responsibility for every action, knowing that its sequential place is part of its very essence?
?
When you consider the sequence of your life—your sins, your repentance, your good deeds—do you treat their order as just a timeline, or do you recognize that your choices create an intrinsic priority and posteriority that cannot be undone by time alone? How will this truth change the way you approach your next decision?

The Eleventh Proof: Time Cannot Exist
The eleventh proof arguing that time cannot exist as a measure of motion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the eleventh proof argues that time cannot be a measure of motion and why its independent existence is impossible.

Core Idea
Time cannot exist independently because its supposed measure has no external reality.

This proof uses a simple dichotomy to show the impossibility of time as an independent entity. By examining both possibilities—that time is a measure of motion or something else—the argument eliminates each. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and its reliance on the nature of extension.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic source and its translation. Notice the logical structure: 'if time existed, then either... or...'.
The passage is tightly reasoned; read it twice.
2
Identify the dichotomy
The argument splits the possibility of time's existence into two mutually exclusive branches: time as a measure of motion, or time as something else. Both are then refuted.
This is a classic 'division and refutation' (taqsim wa ibtal) method.
3
Understand the refutation of the first branch
If time were a measure of motion, it would measure the extension of motion. But extension of motion has no external existence—only individual substance-location occurrences exist. Therefore, its measure, being an attribute of a non-existent, cannot exist.
Key concept: 'attribute of the non-existent' (sifat al-ma'dum) cannot be existent.
4
Note the dismissal of the second branch
The second branch (time as something else) is dismissed by appealing to the consensus of Aristotle and his followers, who agree time cannot be other than measure of motion.
This relies on authority; the real work is in the first branch.
5
Draw the conclusion
Since both possibilities are false, the original assumption (that time exists) must be false. Time has no independent existence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الحادية عشر : لو كان الزمان موجوداً ، لكان إما أن يكون مقداراً للحركة وإما أن لا يكون . والقسمان باطلان، فالقول بوجوده باطل . إنما قلنا : إنه يمتنع أن يكون مقداراً للحركة لوجوه كثيرة سيأتي تفصيلها . لكن الذي نذكره الآن : أن الزمان لو كان موجوداً ، لكان عبارة عن مقدار امتداد الحركة. وامتداد الحركة لا وجود له في الأعيان، لأن الحاصل في الأعيان هو حصول الجوهر المعين، في الحيز المعين، فأما تعاقب حصولات الجوهر المعين في الأحياز المتعاقبة ، فذاك لا حصول له في الأعيان . فثبت : أن امتداد وجود الحركة ، لا حصول له في الأعيان ، وإذا كان هذا الامتداد لا حصول له في الأعيان ، كان مقدار هذا الامتداد ، يمنع يكون موجوداً في الأعيان ، لأن مقدار هذا الامتداد ، صفة لهذا الامتداد . فإذا كان هذا الامتداد معدوماً في الأعيان ، امتنع أن يكون مقدار هذا الامتداد موجوداً في الأعيان ، لأن صفة المعدوم يمتنع أن تكون موجودة . وإنما قلنا : إنه يمتنع كون الزمان شيئاً آخر غير مقدار الحركة ، لأنا نتكلم في هذا المقام مع و أرسطاطاليس ، وأصحابه ، وهم قد أطبقوا على أنه يمتنع أن يكون الزمان شيئاً آخر ، غير مقدار الحركة
The eleventh proof: If time existed, it would either be a measure of motion or not. Both divisions are false, so the statement of its existence is false. We say: It is impossible for it to be a measure of motion for many reasons whose details will come. But what we mention now: that if time existed, it would be an expression of the measure of the extension of motion. The extension of motion has no existence in external entities, because what is obtained in external entities is the obtaining of the particular substance in the particular location. As for the succession of the obtaining of the particular substance in successive locations, that has no obtaining in external entities. So it is established: that the extension of the existence of motion has no obtaining in external entities. And if this extension has no obtaining in external entities, then the measure of this extension prevents it from being existent in external entities, because the measure of this extension is an attribute of this extension. So if this extension is non-existent in external entities, it is impossible for the measure of this extension to be existent in external entities, because the attribute of the non-existent cannot be existent. And we say: It is impossible for time to be something other than the measure of motion, because we are discussing in this place with Aristotle and his followers, and they have unanimously agreed that it is impossible for time to be something other than the measure of motion.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage presents the eleventh proof against the independent existence of time. The argument proceeds by a dichotomy: if time existed, it would either be a measure of motion or something else. Both are shown false. The first case is refuted by considering that time, if it existed as a measure, would be the measure of the extension of motion. However, the extension of motion has no external existence; only the individual occurrences of a substance in a specific location exist. The succession of these occurrences is not an external object. Therefore, the extension is non-existent externally, and its measure, being an attribute of a non-existent, cannot exist. The second case is dismissed by appealing to the consensus of Aristotle and his followers that time cannot be anything other than the measure of motion. Thus both possibilities are eliminated, and the existence of time is impossible.

Key Terms
الزمان
الحركة
الامتداد
المقدار
الأعيان
صفة المعدوم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that because motion has a measured duration, that duration must be an independent entity.
Correction: This proof shows the measure is merely a mental consideration; the extension of motion has no external existence, so its measure cannot be an independent entity.

Checkpoint
According to the eleventh proof, why cannot time be a measure of motion?
A) Because motion does not exist
B) Because the extension of motion has no external existence
C) Because time is prior to motion
D) Because measure is a substance

Key Takeaway
Time cannot exist independently because its only conceivable basis (the extension of motion) has no external reality, rendering its measure impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You structure your days around hours and minutes, yet this proof claims time has no external reality. How would your attitude toward deadlines, aging, and 'wasting time' change if you truly internalized that time is only a mental construct?
?
If the extension of motion has no existence outside the mind, then your entire sense of duration—from a moment to a lifetime—is illusory. Does this realization frighten you, or liberate you? What would it mean to live as if every moment is a direct act of creation rather than a tick of a cosmic clock?
?
This passage exposes a deep assumption: you believe time is real because you experience it. But the proof says experience is of individual instances, not of time itself. Can you identify one area of your life where you have allowed the illusion of time to control your actions (e.g., procrastination, anxiety about the future)? What concrete step will you take today to break that spell?

The Ninth Proof: Time is Prior to Motion
Al-Razi presents the ninth proof that time is not a property of motion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Razi's argument that time is conceptually independent of motion and not merely a property of it.

Core Idea
Time can be conceived without motion; motion cannot be conceived without time.

Al-Razi presents a powerful thought experiment: even if all motion and celestial bodies are annihilated, our innate reason still affirms duration. This leads to the conclusion that time is not a property of motion but an independent entity. Let's examine his reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once without analysing. Let the argument's flow sink in.
Notice the structure: first the dependence claim, then two evidences for independence.
2
Identify the two main claims
Al-Razi makes two directional claims: (1) motion depends on time for its conception, and (2) time does not depend on motion. Find the sentences that express each.
The phrase 'فثبت: أنه لا يمكن تعقل ماهية الحركة، إلا بعد تعقل ماهية المدة والزمان' states the first.
3
Examine the first evidence: annihilation thought experiment
Consider the scenario where God annihilates all motion and celestial bodies. Al-Razi says our innate disposition still judges that there is a duration—the time of annihilation differs from the time of existence. Reflect on why this shows time is not dependent on motion.
This is a conceptual experiment, not a physical one.
4
Examine the second evidence: inner awareness of time
Even when unaware of celestial motions, we find in our intellect an extended continuous flow, like flowing water. This shows time is directly perceived, not derived from motion.
The analogy of the thread on a sword's edge illustrates part-by-part succession.
5
Synthesize the overall argument
Combine the two parts: motion requires temporal afterness, but time is conceivable without motion. Therefore, time is prior to motion and not a property of it.
This proof supports the Ash'ari view that time is an independent entity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة التاسعة : إنا لا نعقل ماهية الحركة، إلا إذا عقلنا كون المتحرك حاصلاً في حيز، بعد أن كان حاصلاً في حيز آخر. ولذلك فإن جميع العقلاء لا يفهمون من الحركة إلا الانتقال من حيز إلى حيز آخر فيكون الحصول في الحيز الثاني واقعاً بعد الحصول في الحيز الأول. وهذه البعدية ليست إلا البعدية الزمانية، فثبت: أنه لا يمكن تعقل ماهية الحركة، إلا بعد تعقل ماهية المدة والزمان. وأما تعقل المدة والزمان فإنه غني عن تعقل ماهية الحركة. بدليل: أنا لما فرضنا أن الله تعالى أعدم الفلك، وأعدم الكواكب، وأعدم كل الحركات، ففي هذه الحالة لم يقدر عقلنا وفكرنا أن يحكم ببطلان المدة، بل حكمت الفطرة الأصلية، بأنه لا بد وأن يكون وقت الإعدام مغاير لوقت الوجود. وأيضاً: فقد بينا أن حالنا نكون غافلين عن الفلك والشمس والقمر، وسائر الكواكب فإنا نجد في عقلنا أمراً ممتداً مستمراً، يحدث منه شيء فشيء، كأنه الماء السيال الجاري، أو كأنه خيط ألقي على طرف سيف، ثم جرّ. فإن الخيط يلاقي حد السيف جزءاً فجزءاً، فكذا ههنا.
The ninth proof: We do not conceive the quiddity of motion unless we conceive that the moving thing is in a place after having been in another place. Therefore, all rational people understand by motion nothing but the transition from one place to another, so being in the second place occurs after being in the first place. This 'afterness' is nothing but temporal afterness. Thus it is established that the quiddity of motion cannot be conceived except after conceiving the quiddity of duration and time. As for conceiving duration and time, it is independent of conceiving the quiddity of motion. The evidence: When we suppose that God most high annihilates the sphere, the planets, and all motions, in this state our intellect and thought are unable to judge the invalidity of duration; rather, the original innate disposition judges that the time of annihilation must be different from the time of existence. Also, we have shown that when we are heedless of the sphere, the sun, the moon, and all the stars, we find in our intellect an extended continuous thing from which something arises successively, like flowing water, or like a thread thrown on the edge of a sword and then pulled. For the thread meets the sword's edge part by part, so likewise here.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage presents the ninth proof that time (al-madda) is distinct from motion (al-haraka) and not a property of it. Al-Razi begins by stating that we cannot conceive motion without conceiving a thing moving from one place to another, and the 'afterness' (al-ba'diyya) involved is temporal. Therefore, motion depends on time for its conception. Then he argues the converse: time can be conceived without motion. He offers two pieces of evidence: first, if we imagine God annihilating all motion and celestial bodies, our innate disposition (al-fitrat al-asliyya) still affirms duration — the time of annihilation is distinct from the time of existence. Second, even when we are unaware of celestial motions, we find in our intellect an extended continuous flow, likened to flowing water or a thread drawn along a sword's edge. This shows that time is an independent concept, not derived from motion. The proof concludes implicitly that time is not a property of motion.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Time is defined by motion and cannot be conceived without it.
Correction: Al-Razi shows time can be conceived even when all motion is annihilated, proving it is an independent concept.

Checkpoint

A) Motion is prior to time.

D) Time and motion are identical.

Key Takeaway
Time is an independent concept that can be conceived without any motion, while motion necessarily depends on time.

The Tenth Proof: Agreement on Priority and Posteriority
Al-Razi uses universal acceptance of priority/posteriority to prove time distinct from motion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Razi uses the universal acceptance of priority and posteriority to prove that time is distinct from motion.

Core Idea
Priority and posteriority exist without motion, proving time is independent of motion.

Al-Razi presents his tenth proof that time is not merely a measure of motion. He appeals to a common ground with those who affirm temporal creation: they all conceive of a 'before' and 'after' relative to the moment of creation, even though no motion existed then. This self-evidential concept of duration shows that time exists independently of celestial motion.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation to grasp the overall argument. Notice the concise style.
Pay attention to the phrase 'before it occurred' as it sets up the key premise.
2
Identify the common premise
Al-Razi begins by stating that those who affirm temporal origination concede that the event was possible before it occurred. This is the common ground he builds upon.
This premise is crucial because it exposes a shared conceptual framework.
3
Follow the reasoning to the conclusion
He then elaborates that regardless of whether the world was possible or impossible before creation, people conceive of priority and posteriority. This shows that time is self-evident and not a property of motion.
The conclusion is that priority and posteriority are due to something other than motion, i.e., time itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة العاشرة : إن القائلين بحدوث الفلك، بل القائلين بحدوث جميع الأجسام، سلموا أن حدوثه قبل أن حدث: ممكن. وهذا يدل على شهادة فطرتهم الأصلية بأنه لا يعقل حدوث شيء، إلا في مدة وزمان. وتمام التقرير في هذا الوجه: إن من القائلين بحدوث العالم، منهم من قال: إن العالم قبل حدوثه كان ممكن الوجود. ومنهم من قال: كان ممتنع الوجود. وعلى التقديرين فقد عقلوا قبل حدوث الفلك والكواكب والعالم قبلاً وبعداً، وذلك يدل على أن جزم العقل بوجود هذه المدة جزم بديهي، وإن هذا القبل والبعد إنما يحصل بشيء سوى الحركة الفلكية.
The tenth proof: Those who affirm the temporal origination of the sphere, indeed those who affirm the temporal origination of all bodies, concede that its occurrence before it occurred was possible. This indicates the testimony of their original innate disposition that no thing is conceived to occur except in a duration and time. The complete exposition of this aspect: Among those who affirm the temporal origination of the world, some say the world before its origination was possible of existence, and some say it was impossible of existence. In both cases, they conceived before the origination of the sphere, planets, and world a priority and posteriority. This indicates that the mind's certainty of the existence of this duration is a self-evident certainty, and that this priority and posteriority occur only by something other than celestial motion.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage presents the tenth proof that time is not a property of motion. Al-Razi appeals to the common agreement among those who affirm the temporal origination (huduth) of the world. These philosophers concede that before the world existed, its existence was either possible or impossible. In either case, they conceive of a 'before' (qabl) and an 'after' (ba'd) relative to the moment of creation. This priority and posteriority are temporal, and they are conceived even when no motion exists (since before creation there was no motion). Therefore, time (al-mudda) must be something distinct from celestial motion (haraka falakiyya). The certainty of time's existence is self-evident (badihi) according to al-Razi. He thus refutes the idea that time is merely a measure of motion.

Key Terms
الحدوث
المدة
الزمان
القبل
البعد
البديهي
الحركة الفلكية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The concept of 'before creation' is merely a logical priority, not a temporal one.
Correction: Al-Razi argues that priority and posteriority are conceived temporally, as the mind's certainty of duration is self-evident, and this is independent of motion.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Time is a self-evident duration that exists independently of motion, as shown by the universal conception of priority and posteriority before creation.

The Eleventh Proof: First and Last of Motion vs. Time
Al-Razi contrasts the effects of positing a first or last for motion versus for time.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why positing a first or last for time necessarily implies prior or subsequent time, while for motion it does not, and how this establishes time as distinct from motion.

Core Idea
Time cannot be bounded without generating more time; motion can.

Al-Razi's eleventh proof uses a clever comparison: when we imagine a beginning or end for motion, no further motion is forced, but for time, a beginning or end always implies more time. This logical asymmetry reveals that time (al-mudda) is a distinct reality, not just an attribute of motion. Let's examine the argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without overthinking. Then read the translation. Notice how Al-Razi presents two parallel cases: motion and time.
The structure is: (1) positing first/last for motion → no regress; (2) positing first/last for time → regress.
2
Identify the key contrast
Focus on the difference between motion and time when boundaries are posited. For motion, a first does not force a prior motion; for time, a first forces a prior time. Understand why – because priority (qabliyya) itself is a temporal concept.
3
Grasp the conclusion
Al-Razi concludes that since motion boundaries do not regress but time boundaries do, time must be something distinct from motion and its properties.
This argument is a classic kalam proof for the reality of time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الحادية عشر : إنا إذا فرضنا أولاً للحركة، فإنه لا يلزم من مجرد فرض أول للحركة، حصول حركة قبل تلك الحركة، لأنه لا يستبعد في العقل أن يكون الشيء ساكناً ثم يتحرك. وأيضاً: إذا فرضنا آخراً للحركة، فإنه لا يلزمنا من مجرد هذا الفرض إثبات حركة بعد تلك الحركة، لأنه لا يستبعد في العقل أن يكون الشيء متحركاً، ثم يصير ساكناً. أما إذا فرضنا المدة أولاً، لزمنا من مجرد هذا الفرض، إثبات مدة قبل تلك المدة، لأن المدة لا يكون لها أول، إلا إذا كان عدمها قبل وجودها وتلك القبلية لا يمكن حصولها ولا تعقلها، إلا بسبب المدة. فثبت: أنا متى فرضنا للمدة أولاً، فإنه يلزم من مجرد هذا الفرض كونها موجودة قبل ذلك، وكذلك إذا فرضنا للمدة آخراً فإنه يلزم من مجرد فرض انقطاع المدة كونها موجودة بعد ذلك الانقطاع، لأنه لا يحصل لها انقطاع، إلا إذا حصل عدمها بعد وجودها، وهذه البعدية لا يمكن تعقلها إلا عند حصول المدة، فثبت: أن فرض أول وآخر للحركة، لا يوجب إثبات حركة قبل ذلك وبعد ذلك الآخر، وذلك يدل على أن المدة شيء مغاير للحركة ولجميع صفاتها وأحوالها.
The eleventh proof: When we posit a first for motion, it does not follow from the mere positing of a first for motion that a motion occurs before that motion, because it is not rationally absurd that a thing be at rest then moves. Also, when we posit a last for motion, it does not follow from this mere positing that a motion exists after that motion, because it is not rationally absurd that a thing be moving then becomes at rest. However, when we posit a first for duration, it follows from this mere positing that a duration exists before that duration, because duration has a first only if its non-existence precedes its existence, and that priority cannot occur nor be conceived except by duration. Thus it is established: whenever we posit a first for duration, it follows from this mere positing that it exists before that. Similarly, if we posit a last for duration, it follows from the mere positing of the cutting-off of duration that it exists after that cutting-off, because its cutting-off only occurs if its non-existence occurs after its existence, and this afterness cannot be conceived except when duration occurs. So it is established that positing a first and last for motion does not necessitate proving a motion before that or after that last, and this indicates that duration is something distinct from motion and all its attributes and states.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage presents the eleventh and most incisive proof. Al-Razi compares what happens when we posit a beginning (awwal) or an end (akhir) for motion versus for time (al-mudda). For motion, if we posit a first moment of motion, it does not force us to suppose a motion before that first moment, because it is rationally possible for a thing to be at rest and then start moving. Similarly, a last moment of motion does not force a motion after it, because it is possible for a moving thing to become still. But for time, if we posit a first moment of time, it necessarily implies a time before that first moment, because a first moment of time can only be understood as the beginning of time after non-existence, and that priority (qabliyya) itself is a temporal concept requiring time to conceive. Likewise, a last moment of time implies a time after that last moment because the cessation of time implies time after the cessation. Therefore, positing a boundary for time generates an infinite regress of time, but for motion it does not. This shows that time (al-mudda) is something entirely distinct from motion and its properties. The proof relies on the idea that time has an intrinsic continuity that cannot be bounded without implying further time, whereas motion can begin and end without necessitating prior or subsequent motion.

Key Terms
الأول
الآخر
الحركة
المدة
السكون
القبلية
البعدية
الانقطاع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Time and motion are the same thing, or time is merely an attribute of motion.
Correction: Al-Razi shows that time and motion behave differently when boundaries are posited: motion boundaries do not force a regress, but time boundaries do. This logical difference proves time is a distinct substance.

Checkpoint

B) It entails the existence of a prior duration.

Key Takeaway
The logical asymmetry between motion and time when boundaries are posited proves that time (al-mudda) is a distinct reality, not an attribute of motion.

Time is Not a Property of Motion
Al-Razi summarizes proofs and concludes time is not motion's property.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why al-Razi concludes that time is not a property or measure of celestial motion.

Core Idea
Time is an independent reality, not a measure of motion.

After presenting several proofs, al-Razi delivers his conclusion. He argues that time and duration cannot be reduced to the quantity of celestial motion or any of its properties. This short passage seals the refutation of the Aristotelian view that time is the measure of motion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the forceful language: 'overwhelming proofs' (barahin qahira).
The passage is a conclusion, so it references earlier arguments.
2
Identify the two claims being rejected
Al-Razi rejects first that time is the quantity of motion, then that time is any property or state of motion. Understand the logical extension: if the first is false, the second also falls.
This is a two-step argument.
3
Reflect on the significance
Consider why this matters: al-Razi is severing the link between time and motion, asserting that time exists independently. Contrast with Aristotle's definition.
This is a key move in Islamic philosophical theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فظهر بهذه البراهين القاهرة: أن الزمان والمدة لا يمكن أن يكون عبارة عن مقدار الحركة الفلكية، وإذا بطل هذا بطل أيضاً: أن يكون الزمان عبارة عن صفة من صفات تلك الحركة، وحالة من أحوالها. وبهذا يظهر فساد ...
Thus it becomes clear by these overwhelming proofs that time and duration cannot be an expression of the quantity of celestial motion, and if this is invalidated, it also becomes invalid that time is an expression of a property of that motion or a state of its states. And by this, the corruption of ... appears.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This short passage is the conclusion of the series of proofs. Al-Razi states that the overwhelming (qahira) proofs have shown that time (al-zaman) and duration (al-mudda) cannot be identified with the quantity (miqdar) of celestial motion. He then extends this to any property or state of motion: time is not an attribute of motion at all. The passage ends abruptly, likely indicating that the refutation of the opposing view is completed in the following pages. The key point is that the previous arguments decisively refute the Aristotelian definition of time as 'the measure of motion.'

Key Terms

Refutation of Time as Celestial Motion and Its Self-Subsistence
Refutes the claim that time is celestial motion and establishes its independent existence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that duration (al-mudda) is a self-subsistent entity independent of celestial motion, and that motion only serves to estimate and divide it.

Core Idea
Time exists on its own; motion only measures it.

This passage tackles a fundamental question: Is time merely a product of celestial motion, or does it exist independently? The author refutes the first view and argues for the self-subsistence of duration. Using a simple analogy of clocks, he clarifies that motion only divides pre-existing time, not creates it.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation to grasp the overall argument.
Notice the author's direct refutation style.
2
Identify the opponent's claim and refutation
Find the statement of the opponent that time is the measure of celestial motion, and see how the author declares it invalidated.
The refutation is stated as 'that is what we have invalidated.'
3
Understand the analogy with water clocks
Analyze the example of water clocks and hour-boxes: they do not create time but only divide night and day. This is key to grasping the distinction.
Relate this to celestial motion's role.
4
Grasp the distinction between existence and estimation
The core point: celestial motion has no effect on the existence of duration; it only estimates and divides it into parts like years, months, days, hours.
This refutes the misconception that motion creates time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قول من يقول : إنه عبارة عن مقدار حركة فلك معدل النهار ، لأن مقدار تلك الحركة عبارة عن صفة من صفاتها ، وحالة من أحوالها وذلك مما أبطلناه . فثبت بهذا : أن المدة موجود قائم بنفسه مستقل بذاته، وأنه لا تأثير للحركة الفلكية في وجود المدة والزمان البتة ، وإنما تأثيرها في تقدير هذه المدة بالأجزاء والأبعاض. ومثاله : تقدير الليل والنهار بالفنجانات ، وصندوق الساعات ، فإن تلك الآلات لا تأثير لها في إيجاد الزمان والمدة ، وإنما تأثيرها في تقسيم الليل والنهار بالساعات والأجزاء ، فكذلك تأثير الحركة الفلكية ليس في تكوين المدة وإيجادها ، بل في تقسيمها بالأجزاء والأبعاض ، وهي : السنون والشهور والأيام والساعات. فهذا تقرير مذاهب هؤلاء الذين يقولون : العلم بوجود المدة وبكونها أمراً مغايراً للحركة الفلكية ، ولجميع أحوال هذه الحركة : [ علم ضروري ]
The statement of one who says: 'It is an expression of the measure of the motion of the celestial sphere of the equinox, because the measure of that motion is a description of its descriptions and a state of its states' — and that is what we have invalidated. So it is established by this: that duration (al-mudda) is an entity subsisting by itself, independent in its essence, and that celestial motion has absolutely no effect on the existence of duration and time (al-zaman); rather its effect is only in estimating this duration into parts and portions. And its example is the estimation of night and day by water clocks and the box of hours, for those instruments have no effect on the bringing into existence of time and duration; rather their effect is only in dividing night and day into hours and parts. Likewise, the effect of celestial motion is not in the formation and bringing into existence of duration, but rather in its division into parts and portions, which are: years, months, days, and hours. So this is an exposition of the doctrines of those who say: knowledge of the existence of duration and that it is something different from celestial motion and from all the states of this motion is [necessary knowledge].
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the view that time is merely the measure of celestial motion. The author first states the opposing claim, then declares that it has already been invalidated. He then establishes that duration (al-mudda) is a self-subsistent entity, and celestial motion has no effect on its existence; motion only serves to estimate and divide duration into parts. He gives the analogy of instruments like water clocks that do not create time but only divide night and day. Thus, the author presents this as an exposition of those who correctly hold that knowledge of duration as distinct from motion is necessary (daruri).

Key Terms
مدة (mudda)
زمان (zaman)
حركة فلكية (celestial motion)
تقدير (estimation)
علم ضروري (necessary knowledge)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Time is created by celestial motion and has no independent existence.
Correction: Celestial motion only divides and measures pre-existing duration; it does not create it.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what effect does celestial motion have on duration (al-mudda)?
A) It creates duration and brings it into existence
B) It estimates and divides duration into parts
C) It has no effect at all
D) It determines the essence of duration

Key Takeaway
Duration (al-mudda) is a self-subsistent entity; celestial motion only divides and measures it, not creates it.

?
The author says knowledge that time is distinct from motion is necessary (ḍarūrī). Do you know this in your heart, or just your mind? What habit shows that you act as if time were only a product of motion?

Circularity Objection and Rebuttal Regarding Time
Author presents a circularity objection and refutes a counter-argument about time's essence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author defends against a circularity objection by distinguishing between proving existence and proving essence.

Core Idea
Proving existence cannot rely on premises that already assume existence.

This passage presents a classic circularity objection in arguments about time. The author skillfully dismantles an attempted escape by showing that the opponent's proof fails to distinguish between establishing existence and detailing essence. Follow along to see how logical rigor prevents hidden assumptions.

Guided Path
1
Understand the dilemma
The author presents two possibilities: either the opponent already knows time's existence or needs inference. Notice the logical fork.
This sets up the circularity condition.
2
Identify the circularity
If inference is needed, the premises used to prove time's existence themselves require prior knowledge of time's existence, creating a loop.
Circularity (دور) is the key logical fallacy here.
3
Examine the opponent's escape
The opponent claims time's existence is known by intuition, only the essence is proven by inference, so no circularity.
The opponent tries to split existence from essence.
4
See the rebuttal
The author argues that the inference provided only shows existence, not the specific essence, so the proof still presupposes existence and circularity remains.
This refutation is the climax of the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو محتاجاً إلى الاستدلال. فإن كان الأول كان الخوض في هذا الدليل غنياً عنه، وإن كان الثاني فنقول : إنكم إنما بينتم وجود الزمان بهذه المقدمات وقد بينا أنه لا يمكن إثبات هذه المقدمات إلا بعد العلم بوجود الزمان ، فيلزم الدور ، ومعلوم أنه باطل . لا يقال : وجود أصل الزمان معلوم بالبديهة ، فأما بيان ماهيته على التفصيل فذاك معلوم بالاستدلال، ونحن إنما أثبتنا بهذا الدليل تفصيل ماهيته ، وحينئذ يسقط الدور. لأنا نقول : إن هذا القدر الذي سبق ذكره من الاستدلال ، لا يدل على بيان ماهيته المعينة وحقيقته المخصوصة ، بل لا دلالة فيه إلا على كونه أمراً موجوداً في الأعيان ، وحينئذ يعود الدور المذكور
Or being in need of inference. If the first, then engaging in this proof is unnecessary. If the second, then we say: You have only established the existence of time through these premises, and we have shown that these premises cannot be proven except after knowledge of the existence of time, so circularity follows, and it is known to be invalid. It should not be said: The existence of time itself is known by intuition, but the detailed explanation of its essence is known by inference, and by this proof we have only established the detail of its essence, and thus circularity ceases. For we say: This amount of inference that was mentioned earlier does not indicate the specific essence and particular reality of time, but rather indicates only that it is something existent in external reality, and then the aforementioned circularity returns.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer unit. The author first presents a dilemma: either the opponent already knows the existence of time or needs proof. If they already know, discussing the proof is useless. If they need proof, then the proof relies on premises that themselves require knowledge of time's existence, resulting in circularity. Then the author anticipates a counter-objection: 'The existence of time is known by intuition; only the detailed essence is proven, so no circularity.' The author refutes this by arguing that the proof given does not establish the specific essence of time, only that time exists in reality. Therefore, since the proof tries to prove existence but presupposes it, the circularity remains. The argument flows logically: the opponent's attempt to escape circularity fails because the proof offered does not provide new detail beyond existence.

Key Terms
دور (circularity)
بديهة (intuition)
استدلال (inference)
ماهية (essence)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that proving the essence of time avoids circularity because existence is known separately.
Correction: The author shows that the proof offered only proves existence, not essence, so the circularity remains unless the proof provides new information about essence.

Checkpoint
Why does the author say the circularity objection remains even after the opponent claims time's essence is proven by inference?
A) Because the opponent's proof does not establish the essence, only existence.
B) Because time is unknowable.
C) Because the opponent used an invalid premise.
D) Because the opponent did not answer the first objection.

Key Takeaway
Circularity arises when proving existence relies on premises that already assume that existence, regardless of claims about essence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about the beginning of time, do you unconsciously assume that time exists in order to prove that it began? How does this lesson reveal a hidden assumption in your own reasoning?
?
Have you ever defended a belief using an argument that, upon examination, assumes what you are trying to prove? What would it cost you to honestly check your premises?
?
This lesson shows that even a distinction between essence and existence can hide circularity. Is there an area of your faith where you rely on a similar distinction to avoid facing a logical flaw? Will you investigate it today?

Time Is Not Subject to Increase or Decrease
Author argues time cannot be subject to increase/decrease, refuting a proof for its existence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the author argues that time cannot be subject to increase or decrease, and how this refutes a proof for time's existence.

Core Idea
Increase and decrease apply only to mental time, not to real time.

This passage presents a second objection against a proof that seeks to establish the existence of time as a real entity. The author points out a critical flaw: the opponent's own principle that only existent things can have increase and decrease, when applied to time, leads to a contradiction. By carefully distinguishing between mental conceptions and external realities, the author exposes the fallacy.

Guided Path
1
Understand the opponent's principle
The opponent holds that only existing things can be subject to increase and decrease. They used this to argue that motions must have a beginning (time).
2
Examine the nature of time
Time is transient; its parts have no permanence. Therefore, it cannot be truly judged to increase or decrease in reality.
Only the mental image of time can be so judged.
3
Recognize the fallacy
The author concludes that what the opponent wants to prove (real time) cannot be the subject of increase/decrease, and the mental subject does not prove real existence. Hence the argument is fallacious.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والسؤال الثاني على هذا الدليل : إن من مذهبكم أن المحكوم عليه بالزيادة والنقصان ، لا بد وأن يكون موجوداً . وبه أجبتم عن دليل من استدل على أن للحركات أولاً بسبب كونها قابلة للزيادة والنقصان ، ثم إن من المعلوم من الأمور المنقضية ، التي لا ثبات لأجزائها ، ولا استقرار لأقسامها ، وإذا كان كذلك ، فحينئذ لا يصح الحكم عليه بالزيادة والنقصان في نفس الأمر . بل غاية ما في الباب : أن الأمر الممتد المرتسم منه في الوهم ، يمكن الحكم عليه بالزيادة والنقصان ، وأما الأمر الممتد من الزمان ، فلا وجود له البتة في الأعيان. وإذا ثبت هذا فنقول : الأمر الذي تريدون إثباته وهو وجود الزمان في الأعيان فإنه لا يمكن الحكم عليه بكونه قابلا للزيادة والنقصان . والذي صدق عليه هذا الحكم، وهو الأمر المفروض في الذهن فإنه لا يدل على كون الزمان موجوداً في الأعيان . فثبت أن هذه الحجة مغالطة .
The second question against this proof: It is from your doctrine that that which is judged to have increase and decrease must be existent. And by this you answered the proof of one who argued that motions have a beginning because they are susceptible to increase and decrease. Then, it is known that time is among the transient things whose parts have no permanence and whose divisions have no stability. If this is so, then it is not correct to judge it as having increase and decrease in reality. Rather, the utmost in the matter is that the extended thing imagined from it in the mind can be judged to have increase and decrease. As for the extended thing of time, it has no existence at all in external reality. And if this is established, then we say: The thing you wish to prove, namely the existence of time in external reality, cannot be judged to be susceptible to increase and decrease. And that which this judgment applies to, namely the thing supposed in the mind, does not indicate that time is existent in external reality. So it is established that this argument is a fallacy.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage presents a second objection against the proof for time's existence. The author identifies the opponent's principle: for something to be subject to increase or decrease, it must exist. The opponent used this to argue that motions must have a beginning (time) because they are susceptible to increase/decrease. The author then argues that time itself is transient, its parts have no permanence. Therefore, it cannot be judged to have increase/decrease in reality. At most, the mental conception of time can be judged so, but the real extended time has no existence. Thus, the object of the opponent's proof—real time—cannot be the subject of increase/decrease, and the mental subject does not prove real existence. Hence, the argument is fallacious.

Key Terms
زيادة (increase)
نقصان (decrease)
منقضية (transient)
وهم (imagination)
أعيان (external realities)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Time as a real entity is subject to increase and decrease.
Correction: Only the mental image of time can be judged as having increase/decrease; real time is transient and lacks stable parts for such judgments.

Checkpoint
What is the main point of the second objection?
A) Time does not exist at all.
B) Increase/decrease apply only to mental time, not real time.
C) Motions are not susceptible to increase/decrease.
D) The opponent's proof is circular.

Key Takeaway
Time, being transient, cannot be truly subject to increase or decrease; only its mental representation can.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You just learned that real time has no stability and that what you measure as 'time passing' is merely a mental construct. How much of your daily worry is tied to a mental timeline of the past and future that has no external reality? Are you willing to release that imagined timeline and live in the only moment that truly exists—the present, where God meets you?
?

Will you let these mental illusions keep you from turning to Allah with a clean slate right now, or will you step out of the imaginary timeline and seek His forgiveness in this very moment?
?

How can you instead see that your Lord is the only reality, and that your tasks and deadlines are merely events He creates moment by moment? Will you trust His timing rather than your mental clock?

The Objection from Time: Infinite Regress of Potentials
Author presents first sub-objection and rebuttal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the opponent's argument about time's own potential leads to an infinite regress and how the author responds by appealing to symmetry with motion.

Core Idea
Time's own potential forces an infinite regress.

This lesson examines the first sub-objection of the third question. The opponent turns the author's proof against itself by applying the same reasoning to time itself. We will see how the author replies by pointing out the parity with motion, undermining the objection.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation. Let the author's structured objection-and-response come through.
Notice the logical flow: premise → infinite regress → opponent's counter → author's rebuttal.
2
Understand the core argument
The opponent argues that between any time's beginning and end, there exists a potential (possibility) of the same magnitude. This potential would itself require another time to contain it, leading to an infinite regress.
This mirrors the proof used against temporal events.
3
Analyze the author's response
The author anticipates the rebuttal that the potential is just an estimative or imaginative construct. He retorts that the same would apply to motion, which is the basis of the opponent's original proof.
The symmetry argument shows the objection is self-refuting.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والسؤال الثالث : هذا الدليل معارض بأمور : أحدها : إن ما ذكرتموه معارض بنفس الزمان ، فإن بين ابتداء كل زمان وبين انتهائه ، إمكاناً يتسع بمثل ذلك المقدار ، ولا يمتلىء بما هو أصغر منه ، ولا يتسع لما هو أعظم منه ، وإمكاناً آخر أقل منه ، لذلك ولا يتسع الزمان ، ولا لما هو أعظم منه ، ويمتلىء ببعضه ، وإذا كان كذلك لزم أن يكون للزمان زمان آخر ، إلى غير النهاية. فإن قلتم : إن ذلك من عمل الوهم وحكم الخيال . فقولوا بمثله في الحركة إذ لا فرق
The third question: This proof is opposed by matters: One of them: That which you have mentioned is opposed by time itself. For between the beginning of every time and its end there is a potential that extends by that same amount, and it is not filled by what is smaller than it, nor does it extend to what is greater than it, and another potential smaller than it. Therefore, time does not extend, nor to what is greater than it, and it is filled by part of it. If this is so, it necessitates that time has another time, ad infinitum. If you say: That is from the operation of estimation and the judgment of imagination. Then say the same concerning motion, for there is no difference.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage is the first sub-objection of the third question, and it is an objection-and-answer pair embedded. The author argues that the opponent's proof is self-refuting when applied to time itself. Specifically, between the beginning and end of any time interval, there exists a potential (possibility) that is exactly the same size as that interval. This potential is not filled by anything smaller, nor does it extend to anything larger. This potential would itself require another time to contain it, leading to an infinite regress. The opponent may respond that this potential is merely an estimative or imaginative construct. The author then retorts: if that is the case, then the same should be said about the motion that the opponent uses in their proof, because there is no difference between the two cases. Thus, the opponent's argument is undermined.

Key Terms
إمكان
وهم
خيال
الزمان
حركة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The infinite regress of times is harmless or merely conceptual.
Correction: The objection shows that the regress invalidates the opponent's original proof, which relied on the impossibility of infinite regress.

Checkpoint
What does the first sub-objection conclude about time?
A) Time is finite.
B) Every time requires another time, leading to infinite regress.
C) Motion is eternal.
D) Potential is not real.

Key Takeaway
The opponent's own argument applied to time leads to an infinite regress, and the author's rebuttal by parity with motion shows the objection fails.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When an argument challenges your deeply held beliefs, do you dismiss it as 'just imagination' (wahm) to avoid discomfort? The opponent did that here. Where in your life have you done the same, and what would it take to honestly engage with that challenge?
?
Are you consistent in applying logical standards to your own arguments and to those of others? The author forced parity between time and motion. Think of a recent disagreement: did you apply the same critical lens to your own position as you did to the other's? Commit to doing so next time.
?
The potential in time leads to an infinite regress. Time is fleeting — every moment contains potential that passes. How does the awareness of time's finite nature and the infinite regress beyond it stir you to use your remaining moments for what truly matters to your Creator?

Future Time Already Present Now
Second sub-objection against the proof: future time would have to be present now.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second sub-objection against the argument that time must exist for past motion, and the dialectical exchange that follows.

Core Idea
The opponent's reasoning would absurdly require future time to be present now.

This passage presents the second part of the third objection. The author argues that the same reasoning used to claim time existed for past motion would force future time to be present now, which is clearly impossible. The opponent attempts to escape by distinguishing potential from container, but the author counters by questioning why the same escape wouldn't apply to the past.

Guided Path
1
Read the full Arabic passage
First, read the Arabic passage straight through. Notice the flow of the argument: statement of opposition, development of the absurd consequence, the opponent's attempted reply, and the author's rebuttal.
The passage is short but dense; read slowly.
2
Identify the two sides
Identify the opponent's original position (that time must be present for past motion) and how the author turns it against the future.
Note the symmetry: the same logic applied to future yields an absurdity.
3
Analyze the rebuttal
Examine the opponent's response: only potential exists now, not an actual container. Then the author's counter: if that works for future, why not for past? This refutes the opponent's objection.
Understand the dialectical move: the author does not accept the opponent's distinction without reciprocity.
4
Consider the implication
Think about why this whole argument matters: it undermines a key objection against the Ash'ari proof from huduth.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وثانيها : إن ما ذكرتموه معارض بجانب المستقبل ، وذلك لأن الساعة الحاضرة إلى الغد ، حصل إمكان يتسع لمقدار من الحركة الموصوفة بمقدار معين من السرعة أو البطء ، ولا يمتلىء بالأقل منه ولا يتسع للأعظم منه ، وإمكان آخر أصغر منه . فهذا يقتضي أن يكون الزمان الذي سيجيء غداً ، حاصلا الآن ، وحاضراً في هذا الوقت. ومعلوم أن ذلك باطل . فإن قالوا : الحاضر في الحال إنما هو إمكان وجود تلك الحركات المستقبلية ، لا وجود شيء آخر يكون وعاء لها وظرفاً لها. فنقول : فلم لا يجوز أن يكون الحال في الماضي مثل ما ذكرتموه في المستقبل ؟
And the second of them: That which you have mentioned is opposed by the side of the future. That is because from the present hour to tomorrow, there obtains a potential that extends to an amount of motion described by a specific measure of speed or slowness, and it is not filled by what is less than it, nor does it extend to what is greater than it, and another potential smaller than it. This necessitates that the time which will come tomorrow is already obtained now and present at this time. And it is known that this is false. If they say: What is present now is only the potential for the existence of those future motions, not the existence of something else that is a container and vessel for them. Then we say: Why is it not permissible that the case concerning the past be like what you have mentioned concerning the future?
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This is the second sub-objection against the proof. It targets the future side. The author argues that from the present moment to tomorrow, there is a potential that exactly corresponds to the amount of motion (with a certain speed) that will occur. This potential is specific and cannot be filled by less or extend to more. This would imply that the future time (tomorrow) is already existent now, which is absurd. The opponent may respond that the potential is simply the potential for the future motions, not a container. The author then turns the argument: if that is so, why not say the same about the past? (Implying that the opponent's reasoning about the past would also be invalid.)

Key Terms
مستقبل (future)
إمكان (potential)
وعاء (container)
ظرف (vessel)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that potential for future motion is the same as an actual container of time.
Correction: The author and opponent both distinguish potential from container; the argument hinges on whether the past case is symmetric.

Checkpoint
What absurd consequence does the second sub-objection derive from the opponent's argument?
A) That time is circular.
B) That future time must already exist now.
C) That motion is infinite.
D) That potential does not exist.

Key Takeaway
The second sub-objection exposes that the opponent's reasoning would absurdly require future time to be present now, and the author's counter-response shows the symmetry that defeats the objection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Are there ways you try to 'possess' the past or future in your heart? What would it mean to let go of that possession and trust that only God encompasses all time?

Spatial Analogy Refutes Vessel Argument
Third sub-objection: spatial potential would require self-subsisting dimensions if analogy with time holds

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author uses a spatial analogy to challenge the opponent's claim that potential for motion implies an existent time-container.

Core Idea
Not every potential implies a container; sometimes it's just the thing itself.

In this passage, the author presents a clever analogy: the potential between the sides of a basin. If the opponent's logic holds, then spatial dimensions would be real entities, which they deny. This exposes an inconsistency in their reasoning. Let's read carefully and see how the author turns their own argument against them.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Notice the argument's flow: an analogy, an opponent's response, and a counter.
The author uses a concrete object (basin) to make the abstract point clearer.
2
Identify the spatial analogy
The author imagines a basin with a potential that can hold a specific amount of bodies. Ask: Why does this analogy help against the opponent?
The key is that the opponent would deny that this potential implies a real container, but they accept it for time.
3
Understand the opponent's reply
The opponent says the potential in the basin is just the potential for the bodies themselves, not a container. Grasp this nuance.
4
See the author's counter
The author then applies the same logic to the opponent's own argument: the potential for motions should likewise be just potential for motions, not a container called time.
This reveals the inconsistency: the opponent cannot have it both ways.
5
Synthesize the refutation
Summarize why this analogy effectively undermines the opponent's third sub-objection. The author shows that the opponent's reasoning leads to absurdities if applied uniformly.
This completes the lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وثالثها : أن نقول : إن بين طرفي الطاس ، إمكاناً يتسع لمقدار معين من الأجسام ولا يمتلء بأقل من ذلك القدر، ولا يتسع للأزيد منه ، فوجب أن يكون ذلك الإمكان الذي يتسع لذلك القدر من الجسم أمراً موجوداً . وذلك يوجب عليكم الاعتراف بوجود أبعاد قائمة بذواتها تكون هي أمكنة لهذه الأجسام . فإن قالوا : ذلك الإمكان عبارة عن إمكان وجود تلك الأجسام في أنفسها ، لا عن إمكان وجود شيء يكون ذلك الشيء ظرفاً لتلك الأجسام ووعاء لها . فنقول : فلم لا يجوز أن يكون الحال فيما ذكرتم ، كالحال ههنا ؟ وهو أن يقال : الإمكان الذي ذكرتم إشارة إلى إمكان وجود تلك الحركات المختلفة في أنفسها ، فأما إثبات أمر آخر ظرفاً لتلك الحركات ووعاء لها . فهذا ممنوع .
And the third of them: that we say: Between the two sides of a basin there is a potential that extends to a specific amount of bodies and it is not filled by less than that amount, nor does it extend to more than it. Thus, it becomes necessary that that potential which extends to that amount of body be something existent. This would oblige you to acknowledge the existence of self-subsisting dimensions that are places for these bodies. If they say: That potential is an expression of the potential for the existence of those bodies in themselves, not the potential for the existence of something that is a vessel for those bodies and a container for them. Then we say: Why is it not permissible that the case concerning what you mentioned be like the case here? That is, it should be said: The potential you mentioned refers to the potential for the existence of those different motions in themselves. As for proving something else as a vessel for those motions and a container for them, this is prohibited.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This is the third sub-objection. The author uses a spatial analogy: between the two sides of a basin, there is a potential that fits a specific amount of bodies. If we follow the opponent's logic, that potential must be something existent, implying self-subsisting dimensions (places) for bodies. The opponent would likely reject this, saying the potential is just the potential for the bodies themselves, not a container. The author then turns the argument: similarly, the potential for motions should be understood as the potential for the motions themselves, not a container time. Thus, the opponent cannot use the potential to prove an existent time as a container. The answer is a direct refutation: the opponent's claim that the potential implies a container is arbitrary, because the same reasoning in space would lead to absurd consequences they deny.

Correction: The author shows that potential can simply be the potential for the thing itself, without needing a separate container. This is demonstrated by the basin example and then applied to motions.

C) Motion and its speed.

Key Takeaway
The author's spatial analogy reveals the opponent's arbitrariness: if potential for bodies does not require a container, then potential for motions does not require time as a container.
